Malloc site tracking

Malloc data from a 2001/10/30 trunk build

The data below show the sites which do the most memory allocation, sorted by the number of mallocs in a typical run. Only sites doing 100 or more mallocs are shown. I didn't consider the size of the allocated blocks, or temporal patterns of allocation; this is pretty high-level data.

The data were generated for a single run of an optimized build of Mozilla on Mac, just bringing up a single browser window (no profile dialog) showing about:blank, then quitting.

To collect the data, I added stack-walking code to the Mac's malloc implementation, which is the bottleneck for all allocations (new, malloc, calloc, realloc, and NSPR versions of same). This dumped the stack for every malloc (all 368000 of them), resulting in a 600Mb data file. With some intrepid use sort/uniq on Unix, I produced the following data.

What the data mean

Each unique stack which allocates memory 100 or more times appears once in the list, like this: 

2094 operator new(unsigned long, const std::nothrow_t&)
		operator new(unsigned long)
		nsXPIDLCString::PrepareForUseAsOutParam()
		nsComponentManagerImpl::PlatformPrePopulateRegistry()
		NS_InitXPCOM2
		main

That shows that that particular stack allocated 2094 blocks of memory during the startup period. There is no data on block size or longevity.

Compare this with data from 2001/2/8.

Simon Fraser sfraser@netscape.com
